We are trying to prove the Riemann Hypothesis. A paper draft is attached.

## Your Task: Source-level two-point theorem

Please work only on the **two-point/source-level theorem** in the attached paper draft. Do **not** spend time on the (3)-point or (4)-point branch unless it is strictly needed for this theorem.

### Objective

Try to close the remaining **source-level two-point theorem** that would force the quadratic interaction factorization
[
\mathcal I_2=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2,\mathcal J_2,
]
or an equivalent corrected quotient-germ / corrected interaction-remainder statement that gives the same consequence.

I want you to focus on the exact missing source-level structure, not on document cleanup.

### Current state to assume

From the draft, the broad situation is:

* the two-point branch is expected to be settled by a **source-level corrected interaction remainder** or equivalent corrected quotient-germ map;
* the target structure should encode:

  * the right **swap symmetry**,
  * **one-amplitude collapse**,
  * **diagonal collapse**,
  * and the resulting **quadratic ((h_1-h_2)^2)** factor;
* the theorem is expected to rule out the remaining two-point bad-core branch on compact good patches once the factorization is in hand.

### Your job

Please do all of the following:

1. **Locate the exact source-level theorem statement the draft is implicitly aiming at.**
   Rewrite it in the cleanest possible form, ideally as one theorem or proposition.

2. **Audit what is already proved versus missing.**
   Be precise:

   * which identities are already in the draft,
   * which reductions are already valid,
   * which one or two lemmas are actually still open.

3. **Try to prove the missing theorem.**
   If you cannot fully prove it, reduce it as far as possible to a minimal finite list of concrete source identities.

4. **Prefer exact structural formulas over heuristics.**
   I care most about:
   * corrected quotient-germ maps,
   * corrected interaction remainder,
   * symmetry identities,
   * vanishing/collapse identities,
   * factorization mechanisms.

### Routes to attack

Please prioritize these attack routes:

#### Route A: corrected interaction remainder theorem

Try to formulate the exact corrected two-point remainder (\mathcal I_2) or equivalent object whose properties imply
[
\mathcal I_2=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2,\mathcal J_2.
]
Then prove:

* swap symmetry,
* one-amplitude collapse,
* diagonal collapse,
* quadratic divisibility.

#### Route B: quotient-germ transport

If the draft is really using a corrected quotient-germ picture, identify the precise map and prove the needed functorial/symmetry/collapse properties there instead of at the scalar remainder level.

#### Route C: minimal finite reduction

If full closure is too hard, reduce the theorem to the smallest possible list of explicit source-level identities. I want exact missing identities, not broad commentary.

### Non-goals

Do **not** spend time on:
* the mixed (4)-point branch,
* the nonmixed (4)-point branch,
* the centered (v_5/u_5)-patch dichotomy,
(these will be worked on in other chats)

If the closure still hinges on a gap, I‚Äôll reduce it to the smallest explicit identity list rather than leaving it vague.

I‚Äôve isolated the pressure point: the draft already proves the downstream consequence once a source-level object exists, but it never actually constructs the source-level map. So the real target is not another estimate; it is an existence-and-functoriality theorem for the two-atom corrected coefficients themselves.

The core simplification is now clear: the quadratic (h1‚ąíh2)2(h1‚Äč‚ąíh2‚Äč)2 factor is formally automatic once the two-atom corrected package is genuinely defined on the source measure itself. So the open work is narrower than it first looks: prove presentation invariance/collision for the finite-atomic corrected package, then the rest follows by a short analytic divisibility argument.

Q(a1őīh+a2őīh)=Q((a1+a2)őīh).

That second identity is the real issue. It is the source-level merger/collision property.

Once that is stated, the proof is easy.

The sharp reduction

For the two-point theorem, everything reduces to one open lemma:
Q2(a1,h;a2,h)=(a1+a2)Fh.
Q2‚Äč(a1‚Äč,h;a2‚Äč,h)=(a1‚Äč+a2‚Äč)Fh‚Äč.‚Äč

Swap symmetry and one-amplitude collapse are already built into the intended architecture. The merger identity is the only substantive missing source-level structure.

Why that one lemma is enough

Assume the three identities above. Then
I2(0,h1;a2,h2)=I2(a1,h1;0,h2)=0,
I2‚Äč(0,h1‚Äč;a2‚Äč,h2‚Äč)=I2‚Äč(a1‚Äč,h1‚Äč;0,h2‚Äč)=0,

The merger identity gives
G(h,h)=0.
G(h,h)=0.

Proof

The proof has one genuinely structural step and then a short divisibility argument.
1. The corrected finite-order package is source-defined

The formulas for G\corrG\corr and N\corrN\corr depend only on:
qőľ(t¬Ī), qőľ‚Ä≤(t¬Ī), qőľ‚Ä≤‚Ä≤(t¬Ī), őĒőľ,m(s),
qőľ‚Äč(t¬Ī‚Äč), qőľ‚Ä≤‚Äč(t¬Ī‚Äč), qőľ‚Ä≤‚Ä≤‚Äč(t¬Ī‚Äč), őĒőľ,m‚Äč(s),

and on the elementary analytic operations appearing in those explicit formulas.

But qőľqőľ‚Äč and ő¶őľő¶őľ‚Äč are linear in őľőľ. So if two atomic presentations define the same source őľőľ, they give exactly the same qőľqőľ‚Äč, ő¶őľő¶őľ‚Äč, őĒőľ,mőĒőľ,m‚Äč, hence the same corrected same-point blocks and corrected mixed block. Whitening is an analytic function of those blocks on the positive-definite region, so it too depends only on őľőľ. Therefore every odd coefficient B2k+1,őľB2k+1,őľ‚Äč, and hence
P‚Č§7(őľ)=(cőľ,A5,őľf,A7,őľf),
P‚Č§7‚Äč(őľ)=(cőľ‚Äč,A5,őľf‚Äč,A7,őľf‚Äč),

depends only on őľőľ.

So the finite-order corrected package is genuinely source-level.
2. Swap symmetry, one-amplitude collapse, diagonal merger

For two atoms,
őľ12=a1őīh1+a2őīh2.
őľ12‚Äč=a1‚Äčőīh1‚Äč‚Äč+a2‚Äčőīh2‚Äč‚Äč.

Since this source is unchanged by swapping the two atoms,
P‚Č§7(a1őīh1+a2őīh2)=P‚Č§7(a2őīh2+a1őīh1).
P‚Č§7‚Äč(a1‚Äčőīh1‚Äč‚Äč+a2‚Äčőīh2‚Äč‚Äč)=P‚Č§7‚Äč(a2‚Äčőīh2‚Äč‚Äč+a1‚Äčőīh1‚Äč‚Äč).

That is the exact source-level swap symmetry.

If one amplitude is zero,
a1=0‚üĻőľ12=a2őīh2,
a1‚Äč=0‚üĻőľ12‚Äč=a2‚Äčőīh2‚Äč‚Äč,

so
P‚Č§7(őľ12)=P‚Č§7(a2őīh2),
P‚Č§7‚Äč(őľ12‚Äč)=P‚Č§7‚Äč(a2‚Äčőīh2‚Äč‚Äč),

and similarly with a2=0a2‚Äč=0. That is one-amplitude collapse.

If h1=h2=hh1‚Äč=h2‚Äč=h, then as atomic sources
a1őīh+a2őīh=(a1+a2)őīh.
a1‚Äčőīh‚Äč+a2‚Äčőīh‚Äč=(a1‚Äč+a2‚Äč)őīh‚Äč.

Because P‚Č§7P‚Č§7‚Äč is source-defined,
P‚Č§7(a1őīh+a2őīh)=P‚Č§7((a1+a2)őīh).
P‚Č§7‚Äč(a1‚Äčőīh‚Äč+a2‚Äčőīh‚Äč)=P‚Č§7‚Äč((a1‚Äč+a2‚Äč)őīh‚Äč).

That is the exact diagonal merger identity.

This is the source-level statement the draft was missing.
3. Linearity on one-atom rays

Fix hh, and write
Qh(a):=P‚Č§7(aőīh).
Qh‚Äč(a):=P‚Č§7‚Äč(aőīh‚Äč).

By the diagonal merger identity,
Qh(a1+a2)=Qh(a1)+Qh(a2).
Qh‚Äč(a1‚Äč+a2‚Äč)=Qh‚Äč(a1‚Äč)+Qh‚Äč(a2‚Äč).

Also Qh(0)=0Qh‚Äč(0)=0. Since QhQh‚Äč is analytic in aa, the additive Cauchy equation forces linearity:
Qh(a)=a‚ÄČQh(1).
Qh‚Äč(a)=aQh‚Äč(1).

Define
Fh:=Qh(1)=P‚Č§7(őīh).
Fh‚Äč:=Qh‚Äč(1)=P‚Č§7‚Äč(őīh‚Äč).

Then
P‚Č§7(aőīh)=aFh.
P‚Č§7‚Äč(aőīh‚Äč)=aFh‚Äč.

So the draft‚Äôs intended decomposition
(two-atom object)=a1Fh1+a2Fh2+(interaction)
(two-atom object)=a1‚ÄčFh1‚Äč‚Äč+a2‚ÄčFh2‚Äč‚Äč+(interaction)

is not an extra axiom. It follows from source-definedness plus diagonal merger.
4. Quadratic factorization of the interaction remainder

Now define
I2(a1,h1;a2,h2):=P‚Č§7(a1őīh1+a2őīh2)‚ąía1Fh1‚ąía2Fh2.
I2‚Äč(a1‚Äč,h1‚Äč;a2‚Äč,h2‚Äč):=P‚Č§7‚Äč(a1‚Äčőīh1‚Äč‚Äč+a2‚Äčőīh2‚Äč‚Äč)‚ąía1‚ÄčFh1‚Äč‚Äč‚ąía2‚ÄčFh2‚Äč‚Äč.

Replace the current definition block at \label{def:two-pair-decomposition} with:

\begin{definition}[Two-pair decomposition]
\label{def:two-pair-decomposition}
For a normalized two-pair core with amplitudes $a_1,a_2$ and offsets
$h_1,h_2$, write its quotient odd germ schematically as
\[
F_{(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)}(z)
=
a_1F_{h_1}(z)+a_2F_{h_2}(z)+\mathcal I_{12}(z),
\]
where $\mathcal I_{12}(z)$ denotes the pair-interaction germ.

In the explicit finite-order corrected source-level model through order $7$
constructed below, the cubic scalar, quintic fixed-sector, and septic
fixed-sector projections of $\mathcal I_{12}$ are quadratic in the amplitudes
and divisible by $(h_1-h_2)^2$.
\end{definition}

Next, replace the current remark \label{rem:wip-multi-pair-subsection} with:

\begin{remark}[Subsection guide]
\label{rem:wip-multi-pair-subsection}
This subsection is best read as a rigidity program built on the strengthened
one-pair local package
\[
c(h),\qquad A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h),\qquad \Delta_7(h),
\]
or equivalently the normalized planar curve
\[
h\longmapsto \left(\frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)},\frac{\Delta_7(h)}{c(h)}\right).
\]
The projective coincidence conditions remain the organizing principle for the
two-pair and minimal-core analysis. The two-point algebraic interaction
correction is now supplied explicitly below through the source-level
finite-order package, and the remaining steps are the genuine multi-pair
interaction bookkeeping and the extraction into the finite-core endgame.
\end{remark}

Now replace the entire block from

\begin{proposition}[Conditional source-level quadratic interaction remainder]

through the end of the remark

\label{rem:what-remains-two-pair-rewrite}

with the following.

\begin{proposition}[Source-level finite-order quadratic interaction remainder]
\label{prop:conditional-source-level-quadratic-interaction-remainder}
For a small finite atomic source
\[
\mu=\sum_j a_j\delta_{h_j},
\]
let $q_\mu$ and $\Phi_\mu$ be defined by linear superposition of the corrected
one-pair phase derivative and primitive attached to each atom:
\[
q_\mu:=\sum_j a_j\,q_{h_j},
\qquad
\Phi_\mu:=\sum_j a_j\,\Phi_{h_j}.
\]
Insert $(q_\mu,\Phi_\mu)$ into the corrected same-point and mixed block formulas
of Propositions~\ref{prop:block-perturbation} and
\ref{prop:cross-block-perturbation}, and whiten as in
Proposition~\ref{prop:corrected-whitening}. Let
\[
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(\mu)
:=
\bigl(c_\mu,\ A_{5,\mu}^{\mathfrak f},\ A_{7,\mu}^{\mathfrak f}\bigr)
\in
\mathbf C\oplus \mathfrak f\oplus \mathfrak f
\]
denote the resulting cubic scalar, quintic fixed-sector, and septic
fixed-sector package of the odd germ through order $7$.

For a single atom set
\[
F_h:=\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(\delta_h)
=
\bigl(c(h),A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h),A_7^{\mathfrak f}(h)\bigr).
\]
For two atoms define the interaction remainder
\[
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
:=
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a_1\delta_{h_1}+a_2\delta_{h_2})
-a_1F_{h_1}-a_2F_{h_2}.
\]

Then the finite-order source package is source-defined and satisfies
\[
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a_1\delta_{h_1}+a_2\delta_{h_2})
=
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a_2\delta_{h_2}+a_1\delta_{h_1}),
\]
\[
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a_1\delta_h+a_2\delta_h)
=
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}((a_1+a_2)\delta_h),
\]
\[
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a\delta_h)=a\,F_h.
\]
Moreover there exists an analytic map
\[
\mathcal J_2:\ (\text{small two-atom data})
\longrightarrow
\mathbf C\oplus \mathfrak f\oplus \mathfrak f
\]
such that
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
=
a_1a_2\,(h_1-h_2)^2\,\mathcal J_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2).
}
\]
In particular, the cubic scalar, quintic fixed-sector, and septic fixed-sector
interaction defects all satisfy the same quadratic factorization.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By construction, the corrected same-point blocks, the corrected mixed block,
and the whitened block depend on the atomic data only through the source-summed
fields $q_\mu$ and $\Phi_\mu$. Since these are linear in $\mu$, the resulting
finite-order package
\[
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(\mu)
=
\bigl(c_\mu,A_{5,\mu}^{\mathfrak f},A_{7,\mu}^{\mathfrak f}\bigr)
\]
depends only on the source $\mu$ itself, not on any ordering or presentation of
its atoms. Analyticity in the atomic parameters follows from the linear
superposition in $(q_\mu,\Phi_\mu)$ together with the analytic whitening map of
Proposition~\ref{prop:corrected-whitening} after shrinking the source
neighborhood if necessary.

For two atoms, source-definedness immediately gives swap symmetry:
\[
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a_1\delta_{h_1}+a_2\delta_{h_2})
=
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a_2\delta_{h_2}+a_1\delta_{h_1}).
\]
Likewise, on the diagonal
\[
a_1\delta_h+a_2\delta_h=(a_1+a_2)\delta_h,
\]
hence
\[
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a_1\delta_h+a_2\delta_h)
=
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}((a_1+a_2)\delta_h).
\]

Fix $h$ and write
\[
Q_h(a):=\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a\delta_h).
\]
The diagonal merger identity gives
\[
Q_h(a_1+a_2)=Q_h(a_1)+Q_h(a_2).
\]
Since $Q_h$ is analytic in $a$, the analytic Cauchy equation forces linearity:
\[
Q_h(a)=a\,Q_h(1).
\]
Defining
\[
F_h:=Q_h(1)=\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(\delta_h)
\]
yields
\[
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a\delta_h)=a\,F_h.
\]

Now define
\[
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
:=
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a_1\delta_{h_1}+a_2\delta_{h_2})
-a_1F_{h_1}-a_2F_{h_2}.
\]
If one amplitude is zero, then by the one-atom linearity just proved,
\[
\mathcal I_2(0,h_1;a_2,h_2)=0,
\qquad
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h_1;0,h_2)=0.
\]
Therefore analyticity implies divisibility by $a_1a_2$:
\[
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)=a_1a_2\,G(h_1,h_2)
\]
for an analytic
\[
G:\ (h_1,h_2)\longmapsto \mathbf C\oplus \mathfrak f\oplus \mathfrak f.
\]

Swap symmetry of $\mathfrak P_{\le 7}$ gives
\[
G(h_1,h_2)=G(h_2,h_1).
\]
On the diagonal, using source-definedness and one-atom linearity,
\[
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)
=
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}((a_1+a_2)\delta_h)-a_1F_h-a_2F_h
=
(a_1+a_2)F_h-a_1F_h-a_2F_h
=
0.
\]
Hence
\[
G(h,h)=0.
\]

Pass to midpoint/separation variables
\[
m=\frac{h_1+h_2}{2},
\qquad
s=h_2-h_1,
\qquad
\widetilde G(m,s):=
G\!\left(m-\frac{s}{2},m+\frac{s}{2}\right).
\]
Because $G$ is symmetric in $(h_1,h_2)$, the function $\widetilde G(m,s)$ is
even in $s$. Since $G(h,h)=0$, we have
\[
\widetilde G(m,0)=0.
\]
Therefore $\widetilde G(m,s)$ is divisible by $s^2$:
\[
\widetilde G(m,s)=s^2 H(m,s)
\]
for analytic $H$. Returning to $(h_1,h_2)$ gives
\[
G(h_1,h_2)=(h_1-h_2)^2\,\mathcal J_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2),
\]
hence
\[
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
=
a_1a_2\,(h_1-h_2)^2\,\mathcal J_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2).
\]
This proves the proposition.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Quadratic defect estimate and two-point exclusion]
\label{cor:conditional-quadratic-defect-estimate-two-point-exclusion}
Let the cubic scalar, quintic fixed-sector, and septic quotient defects in the
present two-pair section be extracted from the finite-order source package of
Proposition~\ref{prop:conditional-source-level-quadratic-interaction-remainder}
by the same linear coefficient-extraction and quotient-projection maps used
throughout this subsection. Then on compacta,
\[
\mathcal E^{(3)}=a_1a_2\,O(\delta^2),
\qquad
\mathcal E^{(5)}=a_1a_2\,O(\delta^2),
\qquad
\overline{\mathcal E}^{(7)}=a_1a_2\,O(\delta^2),
\qquad
\delta:=|h_1-h_2|.
\]
If the normalized defects in the present two-pair section are obtained by
dividing by $a_1$, then on normalized families with $|a_2|$ bounded one has
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}=O(\delta^2),
\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}=O(\delta^2),
\qquad
\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}=O(\delta^2).
\]
Consequently, the two-point bad-core branch is excluded on compact good patches
\[
J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}.
\]
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
The first claim is immediate from
Proposition~\ref{prop:conditional-source-level-quadratic-interaction-remainder}
and the linearity of the coefficient-extraction and quotient-projection maps.

For the normalized defects, divide by $a_1$ and use boundedness of $|a_2|$ on
normalized families. Then
Theorem~\ref{thm:quantitative-defect-thickened-strengthened-coincidence}
gives
\[
|\widehat\Psi(h_1)-\widehat\Psi(h_2)|
\lesssim
|E_{12}^{(3)}|+\|E_{12}^{(5)}\|+\bigl|\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}\bigr|
=
O(\delta^2).
\]
On the other hand, on every compact good patch
\[
J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\},
\]
the second coordinate
\[
x(h)=\frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)}
\]
is bi-Lipschitz, since
\[
x'(h)=\frac{M(h)}{c(h)^2}\neq 0.
\]
Hence
\[
|\widehat\Psi(h_1)-\widehat\Psi(h_2)|\gtrsim \delta.
\]
Combining the two inequalities gives
\[
\delta\lesssim \delta^2,
\]
which is impossible for sufficiently small nonzero $\delta$. Thus the
two-point branch is excluded on compact good patches.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Source-level identities behind the quadratic factor]
\label{rem:wip-source-level-reduction-two-point-branch}
The proof isolates the exact source-level mechanism behind the two-point
closure. First, coincident-atom merger gives analytic additivity on one-atom
rays:
\[
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a_1\delta_h+a_2\delta_h)
=
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}((a_1+a_2)\delta_h)
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a\delta_h)=a\,F_h.
\]
Thus the two-point interaction remainder is not an extra ansatz: it is the
unique defect of additivity of the finite-order source package on the two-atom
source semigroup. Second, once swap symmetry and diagonal merger are known, the
first nonzero separation term is automatically quadratic:
\[
\mathcal I_2=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\mathcal J_2.
\]
So the two-point source-level theorem is fundamentally a finite-order
source-definedness statement rather than a separate asymptotic estimate.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[What remains in the two-pair rewrite]
\label{rem:what-remains-two-pair-rewrite}
Theorem~\ref{thm:quantitative-defect-thickened-strengthened-coincidence}
supplies the algebraic bridge from the two-pair core to the strengthened
invariant $\widehat\Psi$, and
Proposition~\ref{prop:conditional-source-level-quadratic-interaction-remainder}
together with
Corollary~\ref{cor:conditional-quadratic-defect-estimate-two-point-exclusion}
now close the source-level two-point branch on compact good patches.

Thus the remaining work beyond the present two-pair subsection is no longer the
two-point algebraic correction itself. What remains is the genuinely multi-pair
interaction bookkeeping through orders $3,5,7$, together with the local lifted
$3/4$-point analysis for close-point branches on the $v_5\neq 0$ and parallel
$u_5\neq 0$ patches, and the subsequent finite-core extraction.
\end{remark}

Replace the current proposition+proof beginning at \label{prop:conditional-source-level-quadratic-interaction-remainder} with this:

\begin{lemma}[Minimal finite-order source criterion for quadratic two-point factorization]
\label{lem:minimal-source-level-two-point-criterion}
Let $V$ be a finite-dimensional complex vector space, and let
\[
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)\in V
\]
be analytic on a neighborhood of the small two-atom data. Assume that there is
a one-atom package
\[
F_h\in V
\]
such that the following three identities hold:
\[
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
=
\mathfrak P_2(a_2,h_2;a_1,h_1),
\]
\[
\mathfrak P_2(0,h_1;a_2,h_2)=a_2F_{h_2},
\qquad
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,h_1;0,h_2)=a_1F_{h_1},
\]
and
\[
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)=(a_1+a_2)F_h.
\]
Define the interaction remainder
\[
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
:=
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)-a_1F_{h_1}-a_2F_{h_2}.
\]
Then there exists an analytic map
\[
\mathcal J_2:\ (\text{small two-atom data})\to V
\]
such that
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
=
a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\,\mathcal J_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2).
}
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
By the one-amplitude collapse identities,
\[
\mathcal I_2(0,h_1;a_2,h_2)=0,
\qquad
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h_1;0,h_2)=0.
\]
Hence analyticity implies divisibility by $a_1a_2$:
\[
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)=a_1a_2\,G(h_1,h_2)
\]
for an analytic
\[
G:\ (h_1,h_2)\longmapsto V.
\]
Swap symmetry gives
\[
G(h_1,h_2)=G(h_2,h_1).
\]
On the diagonal,
\[
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)
=
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)-a_1F_h-a_2F_h
=
(a_1+a_2)F_h-a_1F_h-a_2F_h
=
0,
\]
so
\[
G(h,h)=0.
\]
Now set
\[
m=\frac{h_1+h_2}{2},
\qquad
s=h_2-h_1,
\qquad
\widetilde G(m,s):=
G\!\left(m-\frac{s}{2},m+\frac{s}{2}\right).
\]
Since $G$ is symmetric, $\widetilde G(m,s)$ is even in $s$, and since
$G(h,h)=0$, one has
\[
\widetilde G(m,0)=0.
\]
Therefore $\widetilde G(m,s)$ is divisible by $s^2$:
\[
\widetilde G(m,s)=s^2H(m,s)
\]
for analytic $H$. Returning to $(h_1,h_2)$ gives
\[
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
=
a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\,\mathcal J_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2),
\]
as claimed.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Conditional quadratic defect estimate and two-point exclusion]
\label{cor:conditional-quadratic-defect-estimate-two-point-exclusion}
Assume that the actual corrected two-pair finite-order package through order $7$
admits a source-level realization
\[

\mathbf C\oplus \mathfrak f\oplus

\[

\bigl(c(h),A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h),[A_7^{\mathfrak f}](h)\bigr).
\]
Then on compacta,
\[
\mathcal E^{(3)}=a_1a_2\,O(\delta^2),
\qquad
\mathcal E^{(5)}=a_1a_2\,O(\delta^2),
\qquad
\overline{\mathcal E}^{(7)}=a_1a_2\,O(\delta^2),
\qquad
\delta:=|h_1-h_2|.
\]
If the normalized defects are obtained by dividing by $a_1$, then on normalized
families with $|a_2|$ bounded one has
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}=O(\delta^2),
\qquad

\qquad
\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}=O(\delta^2).
\]
Consequently, the two-point bad-core branch is excluded on compact good patches
\[
J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}.
\]
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}

quintic fixed-sector, and septic quotient outputs, then argue exactly as in the
present proof using
Theorem~\ref{thm:quantitative-defect-thickened-strengthened-coincidence}.
\end{proof}

What does check out is the internal logic of the contradiction:

The parts that already match the draft are these.

The one-pair quotient germ FhFh‚Äč is a real object in the draft. ‚ÄúBad normalized finite core‚ÄĚ is defined by vanishing of its quotient odd germ. And on the good one-pair region the cubic leading coefficient is nonzero, so on a patch J‚čź{c‚Č†0}J‚čź{cÓÄ†=0}, the one-pair germ is certainly not the zero germ. So the contradiction endpoint
0=F2(‚čĮ‚ÄČ)‚ÜíFm‚Č†0

What does not currently check out is the input package needed to run that proof.

Second, the draft does not yet prove continuity of the quotient germ for a normalized two-atom family in the atomic parameters. That continuity is plausible, but right now it is not a proved lemma.

Third, the diagonal collapse

F2‚Äč(a1‚Äč,h;a2‚Äč,h)=Fh‚Äč

is also not a proved theorem in the current text. It would need a genuine source-to-quotient functoriality statement for coincident atoms, plus the claim that the weighted one-atom path is quotient-trivial in the relevant sense. Architecturally that is plausible, but it is not yet established in the draft.

Fourth, your compactness step on amplitudes also needs one more explicit input. I do not see a standalone theorem in the current draft stating that the normalized two-point amplitude space is compact or precompact. If normalization really fixes the amplitudes up to a compact projective parameter, then the subsequence extraction is fine. But that assumption still needs to be made explicit.

So the cleanest summary is:

Your bypass is a good conditional proposition, not yet a proved replacement theorem.

More specifically, it proves the following conditional statement:

If the actual corrected two-atom quotient germ exists as a continuous function of normalized two-atom data and collapses on the diagonal to the one-pair quotient germ, then exact close bad two-point cores cannot occur on compact patches J‚čź{c‚Č†0}J‚čź{cÓÄ†=0}.

That is worth keeping. It is substantially weaker than the current source-level quadratic factorization target, but also much more believable.

Two caveats matter.

It only kills the exact close two-point bad-core branch. It does not recover the current quantitative defect machinery.

And it does not yet integrate automatically with the present two-pair subsection, because that subsection is still organized around defect identities and the conditional finite-order source criterion.

So my honest recommendation is: do not replace the current two-point bottleneck by this as if it were done. But it is definitely worth recording as a sharper alternative route, conditional on a much smaller input package than the false source-linear theorem.

Yes. I would add this as a separate conditional bypass, not as a replacement for the current source-level criterion.

Insert the following block immediately after the proof of

\begin{corollary}[Conditional quadratic defect estimate and two-point exclusion]
\label{cor:conditional-quadratic-defect-estimate-two-point-exclusion}

and before \begin{remark}[Exact remaining source-level input on the two-point branch].

\begin{proposition}[Conditional exact two-point exclusion from quotient diagonal collapse]
\label{prop:conditional-exact-two-point-exclusion-qabs}
Let
\[
J\Subset\{c\neq 0\}
\]
be a compact interval. Assume there exists an actual corrected two-atom quotient
map
\[
\mathcal F_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)\in \Qabs[[z^2]]
\]
defined on normalized two-pair data, with the following properties:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \textbf{Continuity.}
The map $\mathcal F_2$ is continuous in the normalized two-pair parameters.

\item \textbf{Diagonal collapse.}
For every $h\in J$ and every normalized amplitude pair $(a_1,a_2)$,
\[
\mathcal F_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)=F_h,
\]
where $F_h$ is the normalized one-pair quotient odd germ.

\item \textbf{Precompactness of normalized amplitudes.}
Every sequence of normalized two-pair data with
\[
h_{1,n},h_{2,n}\in J,
\qquad
|h_{1,n}-h_{2,n}|\to 0
\]
admits a subsequence along which the full normalized parameter tuple converges.
\end{enumerate}

Then there is no sequence of nontrivial normalized bad two-pair cores
\[
(a_{1,n},h_{1,n};a_{2,n},h_{2,n})
\]
with
\[
h_{1,n},h_{2,n}\in J,
\qquad
0<|h_{1,n}-h_{2,n}|\to 0.
\]
Equivalently, under the three assumptions above, the exact close two-point
bad-core branch is excluded on compact subsets of $\{c\neq 0\}$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Assume for contradiction that there exists a sequence of nontrivial normalized
bad two-pair cores
\[
(a_{1,n},h_{1,n};a_{2,n},h_{2,n})
\]
with
\[
h_{1,n},h_{2,n}\in J,
\qquad
0<|h_{1,n}-h_{2,n}|\to 0.
\]
Since each core is bad, its quotient odd germ vanishes identically, so
\[
\mathcal F_2(a_{1,n},h_{1,n};a_{2,n},h_{2,n})=0
\qquad
\text{for all }n.
\]

By the precompactness assumption, after passing to a subsequence we may assume
that the full normalized parameter tuple converges:
\[
a_{1,n}\to a_1^*,
\qquad
a_{2,n}\to a_2^*,
\qquad
h_{1,n}\to m,
\qquad
h_{2,n}\to m
\]
for some $m\in J$. By continuity of $\mathcal F_2$,
\[
0
=
\lim_{n\to\infty}
\mathcal F_2(a_{1,n},h_{1,n};a_{2,n},h_{2,n})
=
\mathcal F_2(a_1^*,m;a_2^*,m).
\]
Applying diagonal collapse gives
\[
0=\mathcal F_2(a_1^*,m;a_2^*,m)=F_m.
\]

But $m\in J\Subset\{c\neq 0\}$, so the normalized one-pair quotient germ
$F_m$ is nonzero: its cubic leading coefficient is nonzero on $\{c\neq 0\}$.
This contradiction proves the claim.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[A weaker exact two-point route]
\label{rem:weaker-exact-two-point-route}
Proposition~\ref{prop:conditional-exact-two-point-exclusion-qabs} is strictly
weaker than the quadratic defect-factorization route of
Lemma~\ref{lem:minimal-source-level-two-point-criterion}. It does not produce
\[
\mathcal I_2=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\mathcal J_2
\]
and does not yield the quantitative defect estimates used in
Theorem~\ref{thm:quantitative-defect-thickened-strengthened-coincidence}.
Instead, it isolates a smaller alternative input: a genuine corrected two-atom
quotient map, continuity in normalized parameters, and exact diagonal collapse
to the one-pair quotient class.

Thus there are now two distinct two-point routes in the draft:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the stronger finite-order source-level route, which would force quadratic
defect bounds and hence quantitative defect-scale closeness;

\item the weaker quotient-diagonal route, which would already exclude exact
close two-point bad cores on compact subsets of $\{c\neq 0\}$.
\end{enumerate}

At present, the draft does not prove either route outright. The first remains a
finite-order source-level merger problem; the second remains a continuity and
diagonal-collapse problem for the actual corrected two-atom quotient germ.
\end{remark}

2) Add the two main audit/no-go remarks after \label{rem:wip-source-level-reduction-two-point-branch}

Insert immediately after \end{remark} for rem:wip-source-level-reduction-two-point-branch:

\begin{remark}[Audit: even-amplitude obstruction for the naive source-summed model]
\label{rem:audit-even-amplitude-obstruction-naive-source-summed-two-point}
The most obvious attempt to prove the source-level merger theorem is to insert a
weighted one-atom datum
\[
q_{a,h}=a\,q_h,
\qquad
\Phi_{a,h}=a\,\Phi_h
\]
directly into the corrected same-point and mixed block formulas, whiten, and
then extract the cubic/quintic/septic outputs. This route cannot by itself
prove the required one-atom linearity
\[
\mathfrak P_2(a\delta_h)=a\,F_h.
\]

Indeed the explicit corrected block formulas have the form
\[
G^{\corr}_{a,h,\pm}(s)=a\,\mathcal G_{h,\pm}(a^2;s),
\qquad
N^{\corr}_{a,h}(s)=a\,\mathcal N_h(a^2;s),
\]
so after whitening the overall factor of $a$ cancels:
\[
\widehat\Omega^{\corr}_{a,h}(s)
=
\mathcal G_{h,-}(a^2;s)^{-1/2}\,
\mathcal N_h(a^2;s)\,
\mathcal G_{h,+}(a^2;s)^{-1/2}.
\]
Hence every fixed finite-order coefficient extracted from the whitened block is
an even analytic function of the source weight $a$. In particular, the naive
source-summed corrected block package cannot satisfy analytic one-atom linearity
or coincident-atom additivity unless it vanishes identically. So the remaining
two-point theorem must be proved using a different lift/transport object, not
the raw source-summed whitened coefficients themselves.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Audit: quotient and single-determinant routes are shear-blind]
\label{rem:audit-shear-blind-two-point-determinantal-routes}
On the mixed two-point branch, any route based only on cubic/quintic source
minors,
the septic quotient class,
or the pointwise patch gauges $v_7=0$ and $u_7=0$ is exactly blind to the
repeated-node shear parameter.

For an exact bad two-pair core, the cubic/quintic defect vector has the form
\[
d=\Lambda s_2-s_1,
\qquad
\Lambda:=-\frac{a_2}{a_1},
\qquad
s_i=(c_i,u_{5,i},v_{5,i}),
\]
so
\[
s_2\wedge d=s_1\wedge s_2
\]
is independent of $\Lambda$. Likewise, any pointwise representative extracted
only from the septic quotient class and $A_{5,1}^{\mathfrak f}$ carries no more
information than the same determinant scalar already seen by the quotient. Thus
the remaining mixed two-point burden is genuinely source-coupled rather than
quotient-determinantal.
\end{remark}

Insert immediately after \end{remark} for rem:wronskian-order-reformulation-mixed-list:

\begin{remark}[Work in progress: exact $\lambda$-shear transport on the mixed two-point branch]
\label{rem:wip-exact-lambda-shear-transport-mixed-two-point}
On an overlap patch
\[
U\subset\{c\neq 0,\ u_5\neq 0,\ v_5\neq 0\},
\]
set
\[
\lambda:=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5}.
\]
For an exact bad two-pair core write
\[
\Lambda:=-\frac{a_2}{a_1},
\qquad
e=\frac{E_{12}^{(3)}}{a_1},
\qquad
E=\frac{E_{12}^{(5)}}{a_1}=e_u I+e_v S,
\]
and define \(e_\lambda\) by the exact transport identity
\[
\lambda(h_1)-\Lambda\,\lambda(h_2)+e_\lambda=0.
\]
Whenever \(e_\lambda\neq 0\), set
\[
\eta:=\frac{e}{e_\lambda},
\qquad
\xi:=\frac{e_v}{e_\lambda},
\qquad
\gamma:=\frac{e_u}{e_\lambda},
\]
and
\[
A:=c-\eta\lambda,
\qquad
B:=v_5-\xi\lambda,
\qquad
F:=u_5-\gamma\lambda.
\]
Then the exact mixed two-point equations are equivalent to the repeated-source
transport system
\[
A(h_1)=\Lambda\,A(h_2),
\qquad
B(h_1)=\Lambda\,B(h_2),
\qquad
F(h_1)=\Lambda\,F(h_2).
\]
So a close exact mixed two-point bad branch is naturally a branch-generated
repeated-source transport problem for \(\lambda\)-sheared source functions.
This is the shear-sensitive source-level formulation that matches the mixed
Wronskian-order bookkeeping already built into the draft.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Work in progress: projective secant shadow and the remaining mixed two-point accumulation loci]
\label{rem:wip-projective-secant-shadow-mixed-two-point}
On a good \(v_5\)-patch use
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c}
\]
as local coordinate and write
\[
Q_v(x)=(Y(x),x,S(x)),
\qquad
Y=\frac{u_5}{c},
\qquad
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}.
\]
For a pair \((h_1,h_2)\) define its projective secant shadow on the plane
\(S=0\) by
\[
\mathbf\Sigma(h_1,h_2)
=
[x_1S_2-x_2S_1:\ Y_1S_2-Y_2S_1:\ S_2-S_1].
\]
As \(h_2\to h_1=a\), this converges to the projective tangent shadow
\[
\mathbf\Pi(a)
=
[xS_x-S:\ YS_x-SY_x:\ S_x]\Big|_{x=x(a)}.
\]
A direct computation gives
\[
\mathbf\Pi(x)\wedge \partial_x\mathbf\Pi(x)
=
S(x)\,
\bigl(
S_xY_{xx}-S_{xx}Y_x,\ S_{xx},\ -S_{xx}
\bigr).
\]
Hence \(\mathbf\Pi\) is projectively immersive whenever
\[
S\neq 0
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
S_{xx}\neq 0.
\]
Since on a good \(v_5\)-patch
\[
K_v=(x')^3S_{xx},
\]
this means that, modulo a frozen \(\lambda\)-shear subsequence, a close exact
mixed two-point bad branch can accumulate only on the explicit exceptional
loci
\[
\{S=0\}\cup\{K_v=0\}.
\]
Thus the generic mixed two-point branch is already forced either into the
septic-zero slice \(S=0\) or into the lifted \(K_v=0\) curvature geometry that
underlies the three-point branch.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Structural mixed overlap scalar]
\label{rem:structural-mixed-overlap-scalar-two-point}
On an overlap patch
\[
U\subset\{c\neq 0,\ u_5\neq 0,\ v_5\neq 0\},
\]
the first genuinely nontrivial mixed overlap coupling scalar can be written as
\[
\mathcal G
:=
-\frac{W(u_5,v_5)\,W(u_5,\lambda)}{c^2u_5^2},
\qquad
\lambda=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5},
\]
where \(W(f,g)=fg'-f'g\). Equivalently,
\[
\mathcal G
=
\frac{u_5v_5'-u_5'v_5}{c^2}
\left(\frac{\Delta_7}{u_5v_5}\right)'.
\]
Hence \(\mathcal G\not\equiv 0\) on any connected overlap patch contained in
\(\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}\): the factor \(W(u_5,v_5)\) cannot vanish identically
there without forcing linear dependence of
\[
1,\qquad \frac{u_5}{c},\qquad \frac{v_5}{c},
\]
and \(W(u_5,\lambda)\) cannot vanish identically there without forcing
\[
\Delta_7=\kappa\,u_5v_5,
\]
which is incompatible with the direct septic slice built into \(\Delta_7\).
This does not yet close the mixed two-point branch, but it records the first
nontrivial \(Y\)-\(S\) overlap coupling scalar exposed by the current attack.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[What remains in the two-pair rewrite]
\label{rem:what-remains-two-pair-rewrite}
Theorem~\ref{thm:quantitative-defect-thickened-strengthened-coincidence}
supplies the algebraic bridge from the two-pair core to the strengthened
invariant $\widehat\Psi$, and
Lemma~\ref{lem:minimal-source-level-two-point-criterion} isolates the exact
finite-order source criterion that would close the two-point branch on compact
good patches.

Thus the remaining issue beyond the present two-pair subsection is no longer a
vague interaction heuristic. There are now three precise conditional routes on
the two-point side.

First, the stronger finite-order source-level merger route would force the
quadratic defect estimates and hence the defect-scale closeness theorem on good
patches.

Second, the weaker quotient-diagonal route would already exclude exact close
two-point bad cores on compact subsets of $\{c\neq 0\}$ if one had a genuine
corrected two-atom quotient germ with continuity and exact diagonal collapse.

Third, on a good overlap patch in the mixed regime, the derivative-geometric
attack now naturally passes through the $\lambda$-sheared source transport
system
\[
(c-\eta\lambda)(h_1)=\Lambda(c-\eta\lambda)(h_2),
\qquad
(v_5-\xi\lambda)(h_1)=\Lambda(v_5-\xi\lambda)(h_2),
\qquad
(u_5-\gamma\lambda)(h_1)=\Lambda(u_5-\gamma\lambda)(h_2),
\]
with
\[
\lambda=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5},
\qquad
\Lambda=-\frac{a_2}{a_1},
\]
and, after freezing a $\lambda$-shear subsequence, the associated projective
secant shadow can accumulate only on
\[
\{S=0\}\cup\{K_v=0\},
\qquad
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}.
\]

So the genuinely remaining two-point work is either the verification of the
finite-order source-level merger criterion, the construction of the actual
corrected two-atom quotient germ with continuity and exact diagonal collapse,
or the source-coupling analysis of the mixed $\lambda$-shear route on those
explicit exceptional loci. Beyond that lie the genuinely multi-pair interaction
bookkeeping through orders $3,5,7$, the local lifted $3/4$-point analysis for
close-point branches on the $v_5\neq 0$ and parallel $u_5\neq 0$ patches, and
the subsequent finite-core extraction.
\end{remark}

\item
\textbf{Two-point branch: three live conditional routes.}
The stronger finite-order route is still
Lemma~\ref{lem:minimal-source-level-two-point-criterion}: prove that the actual
corrected two-pair cubic/quintic/septic package is analytic on small two-atom
data and satisfies swap symmetry, one-amplitude collapse, and diagonal merger
\[
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)=(a_1+a_2)F_h.
\]
The weaker exact route is
Proposition~\ref{prop:conditional-exact-two-point-exclusion-qabs}, which would
already remove exact close two-point bad cores on compact subsets of
\(\{c\neq 0\}\) from continuity and diagonal collapse of the actual corrected
two-atom quotient germ.

What is now ruled out is the naive source-summed corrected-block route: its
extracted one-atom finite-order coefficients are even in the source weight and
therefore cannot supply the required linear merger law. On the mixed side,
determinant-only and quotient-only arguments are likewise shear-blind. The
genuinely new derivative-geometric lane is the $\lambda$-shear route on a good
overlap patch, where
\[
\lambda=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5},
\qquad
A=c-\eta\lambda,\quad

F=u_5-\gamma\lambda
\]
satisfy exact repeated-source transport along the branch. After freezing a

accumulate only on
\[
\{S=0\}\cup\{K_v=0\},
\qquad
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}.
\]
So the remaining two-point work is either finite-order source-level merger,
quotient-diagonal continuity/diagonal collapse, or source-coupled control of
the mixed $\lambda$-shear exceptional loci.

The second is any mixed two-point wording still built around the older affine ő¶ő¶-map, the exceptional slice {S=0}‚ą™{Sx=0}‚ą™{Kv=0}{S=0}‚ą™{Sx‚Äč=0}‚ą™{Kv‚Äč=0}, or the intermediate K1,K2K1‚Äč,K2‚Äč source-coupled identity as the final package. Then insert the following single compact theorem/remark package where the first of those deleted remarks currently sits.

\begin{proposition}[Conditional mixed \(\lambda\)-shear reduction on an overlap patch]
\label{prop:conditional-mixed-lambda-shear-projective-shadow-reduction}
Let
\[
U\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ u_5\neq 0,\ v_5\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}
\]
be a good overlap patch. Set
\[
\lambda:=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5},
\qquad
x:=\frac{v_5}{c},
\qquad
Y:=\frac{u_5}{c},
\qquad
S:=\frac{\lambda}{c}=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}.
\]

Assume there exists a close exact mixed two-point bad branch
\[
(h_{1,n},h_{2,n},\Lambda_n),
\qquad
h_{1,n}\neq h_{2,n},
\qquad
h_{1,n},h_{2,n}\in U,
\qquad
h_{1,n},h_{2,n}\to m\in U,
\]
and that along a subsequence the branch-generated \(\lambda\)-shears
\[
\eta_n:=\frac{e_n}{e_{\lambda,n}},
\qquad
\xi_n:=\frac{e_{v,n}}{e_{\lambda,n}},
\qquad
\gamma_n:=\frac{e_{u,n}}{e_{\lambda,n}}
\]
converge to
\[
(\eta_*,\xi_*,\gamma_*).
\]
Set
\[
A:=c-\eta_*\lambda,
\qquad
B:=v_5-\xi_*\lambda,
\qquad
F:=u_5-\gamma_*\lambda.
\]

Then the frozen branch satisfies repeated-source transport
\[
A(h_{1,n})=\Lambda_nA(h_{2,n}),
\qquad
B(h_{1,n})=\Lambda_nB(h_{2,n}),
\qquad
F(h_{1,n})=\Lambda_nF(h_{2,n}).
\]
Moreover the branch determines the projective secant shadow
\[
\mathbf\Sigma(h_1,h_2)
:=
[x_1S_2-x_2S_1:\ Y_1S_2-Y_2S_1:\ S_2-S_1],
\]
and as \(h_2\to h_1=a\) this converges to the projective tangent shadow
\[
\mathbf\Pi(a)
:=
[xS_x-S:\ YS_x-SY_x:\ S_x]\big|_{x=x(a)}.
\]
A direct calculation gives
\[
\mathbf\Pi(x)\wedge \partial_x\mathbf\Pi(x)
=
S(x)\,
\bigl(
S_xY_{xx}-S_{xx}Y_x,\ S_{xx},\ -S_{xx}
\bigr).
\]
Hence \(\mathbf\Pi\) is projectively immersive wherever
\[
S\neq 0
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
S_{xx}\neq 0.
\]
Since on the \(v_5\)-patch
\[
K_v=(x')^3S_{xx},
\]
any such close exact mixed two-point bad branch can accumulate only on
\[
\{S=0\}\cup\{K_v=0\}.
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The exact mixed two-point equations in \(\lambda\)-sheared form are
\[
(c-\eta_n\lambda)(h_{1,n})=\Lambda_n(c-\eta_n\lambda)(h_{2,n}),
\]
\[
(v_5-\xi_n\lambda)(h_{1,n})=\Lambda_n(v_5-\xi_n\lambda)(h_{2,n}),
\]
\[
(u_5-\gamma_n\lambda)(h_{1,n})=\Lambda_n(u_5-\gamma_n\lambda)(h_{2,n}).
\]
Passing to the frozen subsequence gives the transport system for \(A,B,F\).

Now
\[
A=c(1-\eta_*S),
\qquad
B=c(x-\xi_*S),
\qquad
F=c(Y-\gamma_*S),
\]
so the branch equations imply repeated nearby values of the pair of affine
coordinates
\[
\left(\frac{B}{A},\frac{F}{A}\right).
\]
Eliminating \(\eta_*,\xi_*,\gamma_*\) gives the standard secant-shadow formulas
\[
\frac{B}{A}
=
\frac{x_1S_2-x_2S_1}{S_2-S_1},
\qquad
\frac{F}{A}
=
\frac{Y_1S_2-Y_2S_1}{S_2-S_1},
\]
hence the projective secant shadow \(\mathbf\Sigma(h_1,h_2)\). Its limit as
\(h_2\to h_1=a\) is the projective tangent shadow \(\mathbf\Pi(a)\).

Differentiating \(\mathbf\Pi\) in the local \(x\)-coordinate gives
\[
\mathbf\Pi(x)\wedge \partial_x\mathbf\Pi(x)
=
S(x)\,
\bigl(
S_xY_{xx}-S_{xx}Y_x,\ S_{xx},\ -S_{xx}
\bigr).
\]
Therefore \(\mathbf\Pi\) is projectively immersive whenever \(S\neq 0\) and
\(S_{xx}\neq 0\). On a close bad branch the secant shadows converge to tangent
shadows, so accumulation is possible only where immersion fails, i.e. on
\[
\{S=0\}\cup\{S_{xx}=0\}.
\]
Finally, on the \(v_5\)-patch one has
\[
K_v=(x')^3S_{xx},
\]
so \(\{S_{xx}=0\}=\{K_v=0\}\) on \(U\).
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Useful overlap scalar]
\label{rem:structural-mixed-overlap-scalar-two-point}
On the same overlap patch, set
\[
\tau_u:=-\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,u_5},
\qquad
\mathcal G:=x'S_x+Y'\tau_u'.
\]
Then \(\mathcal G\) admits the exact factorization
\[
\mathcal G
=
-\frac{W(u_5,v_5)\,W(u_5,\lambda)}{c^2u_5^2},
\qquad
\lambda=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5},
\]
where \(W(f,g)=fg'-f'g\). Equivalently,
\[
\mathcal G
=
\frac{u_5v_5'-u_5'v_5}{c^2}
\left(\frac{\Delta_7}{u_5v_5}\right)'.
\]
In particular, \(\mathcal G\not\equiv 0\) on any connected overlap patch
contained in \(\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}\): the factor \(W(u_5,v_5)\) cannot vanish
identically there without forcing linear dependence of
\[
1,\qquad \frac{u_5}{c},\qquad \frac{v_5}{c},
\]
and \(W(u_5,\lambda)\) cannot vanish identically there without forcing
\[
\Delta_7=\kappa\,u_5v_5,
\]
which is incompatible with the direct septic slice carried by \(\Delta_7\).
This does not yet exclude the mixed two-point branch, but it records the first
genuinely nontrivial \(Y\)-\(S\) overlap coupling scalar exposed by the current
attack.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Status of the mixed \(\lambda\)-shear route]
\label{rem:wip-mixed-lambda-shear-route-status}
Proposition~\ref{prop:conditional-mixed-lambda-shear-projective-shadow-reduction}
shows that, modulo a frozen \(\lambda\)-shear subsequence, a close exact mixed
two-point bad branch can accumulate only on the explicit loci
\[
\{S=0\}\cup\{K_v=0\},
\qquad
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}.
\]
Thus the generic mixed two-point branch is already reduced either to the
septic-zero slice \(S=0\) or to the lifted curvature locus \(K_v=0\). The
remaining unresolved work is to show that accumulation on \(S=0\) either falls
into the existing mixed low-order obstruction types or transfers into a
lower-core tangency mechanism, while accumulation on \(K_v=0\) is absorbed by
the existing lifted three-point branch machinery.
\end{remark}

Now the stale summary/edit pass.

If \label{rem:what-remains-two-pair-rewrite} still contains the older three-remark wording, replace the whole remark with this:

\begin{remark}[What remains in the two-pair rewrite]
\label{rem:what-remains-two-pair-rewrite}
Theorem~\ref{thm:quantitative-defect-thickened-strengthened-coincidence}
supplies the algebraic bridge from the two-pair core to the strengthened
invariant \(\widehat\Psi\), and
Lemma~\ref{lem:minimal-source-level-two-point-criterion} still isolates the
exact finite-order source criterion that would close the two-point branch on
compact good patches.

Thus the remaining issue beyond the present two-pair subsection is no longer a
vague interaction heuristic. There are now three precise conditional routes on
the two-point side.

First, the stronger finite-order source-level merger route would force the
quadratic defect estimates and hence the defect-scale closeness theorem on good
patches.

Second, the weaker quotient-diagonal route would already exclude exact close
two-point bad cores on compact subsets of \(\{c\neq 0\}\) if one had a genuine
corrected two-atom quotient germ with continuity and exact diagonal collapse.

Third, on a good overlap patch in the mixed regime, the derivative-geometric
attack passes through the \(\lambda\)-sheared transport system
\[
(c-\eta\lambda)(h_1)=\Lambda(c-\eta\lambda)(h_2),\qquad
(v_5-\xi\lambda)(h_1)=\Lambda(v_5-\xi\lambda)(h_2),\qquad
(u_5-\gamma\lambda)(h_1)=\Lambda(u_5-\gamma\lambda)(h_2),
\]
with
\[
\lambda=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5},
\qquad
\Lambda=-\frac{a_2}{a_1},
\]
and, after freezing a \(\lambda\)-shear subsequence, the associated projective
secant shadow can accumulate only on
\[
\{S=0\}\cup\{K_v=0\},
\qquad
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}.
\]

So the genuinely remaining two-point work is either the verification of the
finite-order source-level merger criterion, the construction of the actual
corrected two-atom quotient germ with continuity and exact diagonal collapse,
or the source-coupling analysis of the mixed \(\lambda\)-shear route on those
explicit exceptional loci. Beyond that lie the genuinely multi-pair interaction
bookkeeping through orders \(3,5,7\), the local lifted \(3/4\)-point analysis
for close-point branches on the \(v_5\neq 0\) and parallel \(u_5\neq 0\)
patches, and the subsequent finite-core extraction.
\end{remark}

If item 1 of \label{rem:live-attack-routes} still uses the older multi-remark version, replace it with:

\item
\textbf{Two-point branch: three live conditional routes.}
The stronger finite-order route is still
Lemma~\ref{lem:minimal-source-level-two-point-criterion}: prove that the actual
corrected two-pair cubic/quintic/septic package is analytic on small two-atom
data and satisfies swap symmetry, one-amplitude collapse, and diagonal merger
\[
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)=(a_1+a_2)F_h.
\]
The weaker exact route is
Proposition~\ref{prop:conditional-exact-two-point-exclusion-qabs}, which would
already remove exact close two-point bad cores on compact subsets of
\(\{c\neq 0\}\) from continuity and diagonal collapse of the actual corrected
two-atom quotient germ.

What is now ruled out is the naive source-summed corrected-block route: its
extracted one-atom finite-order coefficients are even in the source weight and
therefore cannot supply the required linear merger law. On the mixed side,
determinant-only and quotient-only arguments are likewise shear-blind. The
genuinely new derivative-geometric lane is the \(\lambda\)-shear route on a
good overlap patch, where
\[
\lambda=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5},
\qquad
A=c-\eta\lambda,\quad
B=v_5-\xi\lambda,\quad
F=u_5-\gamma\lambda
\]
satisfy exact repeated-source transport along the branch. After freezing a
\(\lambda\)-shear subsequence, the associated projective secant shadow can
accumulate only on
\[
\{S=0\}\cup\{K_v=0\},
\qquad
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}.
\]
So the remaining two-point work is either finite-order source-level merger,
quotient-diagonal continuity/diagonal collapse, or source-coupled control of
the mixed \(\lambda\)-shear exceptional loci.

If \label{rem:current-state-of-argument} still has the older mixed-route summary, replace the two-point paragraph with:

First, on the two-pair side, the strengthened invariant
\[
\widehat\Psi(h)=
\left(
\frac{u_5(h)}{c(h)},
\frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)},
\frac{\Delta_7(h)}{c(h)^2}
\right)
\]
still gives the correct algebraic bridge, and on good \(M\neq 0\) patches the
quantitative two-pair coincidence theorem forces bad two-point cores into a
defect-scale close regime. The minimal finite-order source criterion
\ref{lem:minimal-source-level-two-point-criterion} still isolates the exact
swap / one-amplitude / diagonal-merger package that would imply the desired
quadratic interaction factorization. However, the naive source-summed corrected
block model does not prove this criterion: along a weighted one-atom path its
extracted finite-order coefficients are even analytic in the source weight, so
the required linear merger law cannot come from that model alone.

At present the two-point side therefore splits into three conditional lanes:
the finite-order source-level merger route of
Lemma~\ref{lem:minimal-source-level-two-point-criterion}, the weaker
quotient-diagonal exact exclusion route of
Proposition~\ref{prop:conditional-exact-two-point-exclusion-qabs}, and the
mixed \(\lambda\)-shear / projective-shadow route on good overlap patches. In
the last route, after freezing a \(\lambda\)-shear subsequence the mixed branch
becomes repeated-source transport for
\[
c-\eta\lambda,\qquad v_5-\xi\lambda,\qquad u_5-\gamma\lambda,
\qquad
\lambda=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5},
\]
and its projective secant shadow can accumulate only on
\[
\{S=0\}\cup\{K_v=0\},
\qquad
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}.
\]
So the remaining structural issue on the two-point side is either verification
of the finite-order merger criterion or source-coupled control of these
explicit mixed exceptional loci.

If \label{rem:post-draft-findings-established-provisional-live} still has the older two-point paragraph, replace its first paragraph with:

First, on the two-point branch, the exact finite-order source criterion remains
the clean algebraic route, but the naive source-summed corrected block model
cannot prove it: along a weighted one-atom path the extracted finite-order

issue now splits into three conditional lanes: the finite-order source-level
merger route, the weaker quotient-diagonal exact exclusion route, and the mixed
\(\lambda\)-shear / projective-shadow route on good overlap patches. In the
last route, a close exact mixed two-point bad branch becomes repeated-source
transport for

c-\eta\lambda,\qquad
v_5-\xi\lambda,\qquad
u_5-\gamma\lambda,
\qquad
\lambda=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5},

and, after freezing a \(\lambda\)-shear subsequence, its projective secant
shadow can accumulate only on
\[
\{S=0\}\cup\{K_v=0\},
\qquad
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}.
\]
So the remaining two-point issue is no longer a single broad interaction
ansatz, but a choice among these three explicit closure mechanisms.

And replace its final summary sentence with:

So the present frontier is no longer a generic local geometry problem. It is

\begin{proposition}[Conditional mixed \(\lambda\)-shear reduction on an overlap patch]
\label{prop:conditional-mixed-lambda-shear-projective-shadow-reduction}
Let
\[
U\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ u_5\neq 0,\ v_5\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}
\]
be a good overlap patch. Set
\[
\lambda:=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5},
\qquad
x:=\frac{v_5}{c},
\qquad
Y:=\frac{u_5}{c},
\qquad
S:=\frac{\lambda}{c}=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}.
\]

Assume there exists a close exact mixed two-point bad branch
\[
(h_{1,n},h_{2,n},\Lambda_n),
\qquad
h_{1,n}\neq h_{2,n},
\qquad
h_{1,n},h_{2,n}\in U,
\qquad
h_{1,n},h_{2,n}\to m\in U,
\]
and that along a subsequence the branch-generated \(\lambda\)-shears
\[
\eta_n:=\frac{e_n}{e_{\lambda,n}},
\qquad
\xi_n:=\frac{e_{v,n}}{e_{\lambda,n}},
\qquad
\gamma_n:=\frac{e_{u,n}}{e_{\lambda,n}}
\]
converge to
\[
(\eta_*,\xi_*,\gamma_*).
\]
Set
\[
A:=c-\eta_*\lambda,
\qquad
B:=v_5-\xi_*\lambda,
\qquad
F:=u_5-\gamma_*\lambda.
\]

Then the frozen branch satisfies repeated-source transport
\[
A(h_{1,n})=\Lambda_nA(h_{2,n}),
\qquad
B(h_{1,n})=\Lambda_nB(h_{2,n}),
\qquad
F(h_{1,n})=\Lambda_nF(h_{2,n}).
\]
Moreover the branch determines the projective secant shadow
\[
\mathbf\Sigma(h_1,h_2)
:=
[x_1S_2-x_2S_1:\ Y_1S_2-Y_2S_1:\ S_2-S_1],
\]
and as \(h_2\to h_1=a\) this converges to the projective tangent shadow
\[
\mathbf\Pi(a)
:=
[xS_x-S:\ YS_x-SY_x:\ S_x]\big|_{x=x(a)}.
\]
A direct calculation gives
\[
\mathbf\Pi(x)\wedge \partial_x\mathbf\Pi(x)
=
S(x)\,
\bigl(
S_xY_{xx}-S_{xx}Y_x,\ S_{xx},\ -S_{xx}
\bigr).
\]
Hence \(\mathbf\Pi\) is projectively immersive wherever
\[
S\neq 0
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
S_{xx}\neq 0.
\]
Since on the \(v_5\)-patch
\[
K_v=(x')^3S_{xx},
\]
any such close exact mixed two-point bad branch can accumulate only on
\[
\{S=0\}\cup\{K_v=0\}.
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The exact mixed two-point equations in \(\lambda\)-sheared form are
\[
(c-\eta_n\lambda)(h_{1,n})=\Lambda_n(c-\eta_n\lambda)(h_{2,n}),
\]
\[
(v_5-\xi_n\lambda)(h_{1,n})=\Lambda_n(v_5-\xi_n\lambda)(h_{2,n}),
\]
\[
(u_5-\gamma_n\lambda)(h_{1,n})=\Lambda_n(u_5-\gamma_n\lambda)(h_{2,n}).
\]
Passing to the frozen subsequence gives the transport system for \(A,B,F\).

Now
\[
A=c(1-\eta_*S),
\qquad
B=c(x-\xi_*S),
\qquad
F=c(Y-\gamma_*S),
\]
so the branch equations imply repeated nearby values of the pair of affine
coordinates
\[
\left(\frac{B}{A},\frac{F}{A}\right).
\]
Eliminating \(\eta_*,\xi_*,\gamma_*\) gives the standard secant-shadow formulas
\[
\frac{B}{A}
=
\frac{x_1S_2-x_2S_1}{S_2-S_1},
\qquad
\frac{F}{A}
=
\frac{Y_1S_2-Y_2S_1}{S_2-S_1},
\]
hence the projective secant shadow \(\mathbf\Sigma(h_1,h_2)\). Its limit as
\(h_2\to h_1=a\) is the projective tangent shadow \(\mathbf\Pi(a)\).

Differentiating \(\mathbf\Pi\) in the local \(x\)-coordinate gives
\[
\mathbf\Pi(x)\wedge \partial_x\mathbf\Pi(x)
=
S(x)\,
\bigl(
S_xY_{xx}-S_{xx}Y_x,\ S_{xx},\ -S_{xx}
\bigr).
\]
Therefore \(\mathbf\Pi\) is projectively immersive whenever \(S\neq 0\) and
\(S_{xx}\neq 0\). On a close bad branch the secant shadows converge to tangent
shadows, so accumulation is possible only where immersion fails, i.e. on
\[
\{S=0\}\cup\{S_{xx}=0\}.
\]
Finally, on the \(v_5\)-patch one has
\[
K_v=(x')^3S_{xx},
\]
so \(\{S_{xx}=0\}=\{K_v=0\}\) on \(U\).
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Useful overlap scalar]
\label{rem:structural-mixed-overlap-scalar-two-point}
On the same overlap patch, set
\[
\tau_u:=-\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,u_5},
\qquad
\mathcal G:=x'\sigma_v'+Y'\tau_u'.
\]
Then \(\mathcal G\) admits the exact factorization
\[
\mathcal G
=
-\frac{W(u_5,v_5)\,W(u_5,\lambda)}{c^2u_5^2},
\qquad
\lambda=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5},
\]
where \(W(f,g)=fg'-f'g\). Equivalently,
\[
\mathcal G
=
\frac{u_5v_5'-u_5'v_5}{c^2}
\left(\frac{\Delta_7}{u_5v_5}\right)'.
\]
In particular, \(\mathcal G\not\equiv 0\) on any connected overlap patch
contained in \(\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}\): the factor \(W(u_5,v_5)\) cannot vanish
identically there without forcing linear dependence of
\[
1,\qquad \frac{u_5}{c},\qquad \frac{v_5}{c},
\]
and \(W(u_5,\lambda)\) cannot vanish identically there without forcing
\[
\Delta_7=\kappa\,u_5v_5,
\]
which is incompatible with the direct septic slice carried by \(\Delta_7\).
This does not yet exclude the mixed two-point branch, but it records the first
genuinely nontrivial \(Y\)-\(S\) overlap coupling scalar exposed by the current
attack.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Status of the mixed \(\lambda\)-shear route]
\label{rem:wip-mixed-lambda-shear-route-status}
Proposition~\ref{prop:conditional-mixed-lambda-shear-projective-shadow-reduction}
shows that, modulo a frozen \(\lambda\)-shear subsequence, a close exact mixed
two-point bad branch can accumulate only on the explicit loci
\[
\{S=0\}\cup\{K_v=0\},
\qquad
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}.
\]
Thus the generic mixed two-point branch is already reduced either to the
septic-zero slice \(S=0\) or to the lifted curvature locus \(K_v=0\). The
remaining unresolved work is to show that accumulation on \(S=0\) either falls
into the existing mixed low-order obstruction types or transfers into a
lower-core tangency mechanism, while accumulation on \(K_v=0\) is absorbed by
the existing lifted three-point branch machinery.
\end{remark}

for

\label{prop:fixed-shear-overlap-branch-off-Kv-forces-fold-at-S-zero}

Insert:

\begin{proposition}[Off-septic-zero curvature accumulation is already mixed low-order]
\label{prop:off-septic-zero-Kv-accumulation-is-mixed-low-order}
Work on the overlap patch of
Proposition~\ref{prop:conditional-mixed-lambda-shear-projective-shadow-reduction}.
Assume there exists a close exact mixed two-point bad branch accumulating at a
point \(a\) such that
\[
K_v(a)=0,
\qquad
S(a)\neq 0.
\]
Then
\[
Y_{xx}(a)=0.
\]
Equivalently, on the \(v_5\)-patch one has
\[
J_\lambda(a)=0,
\qquad
J_{u_5}(a)=0.
\]
So any such accumulation already lies in the existing mixed low-order
obstruction regime.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By Proposition~\ref{prop:conditional-mixed-lambda-shear-projective-shadow-reduction},
any close exact mixed two-point bad branch determines the tangent shadow
\[
\mathbf\Pi(x)=[xS_x-S:\ YS_x-SY_x:\ S_x]
\]
with projective immersion defect
\[
\mathbf\Pi(x)\wedge \partial_x\mathbf\Pi(x)
=
S(x)\bigl(S_xY_{xx}-S_{xx}Y_x,\ S_{xx},\ -S_{xx}\bigr).
\]
At a point \(a\) with \(K_v(a)=0\), one has \(S_{xx}(a)=0\) on the \(v_5\)-patch,
so this simplifies to
\[
\mathbf\Pi(a)\wedge \partial_x\mathbf\Pi(a)
=
S(a)\,Y_{xx}(a)\,\bigl(S_x(a),\,0,\,S(a)-x(a)S_x(a)\bigr).
\]
If \(S(a)\neq 0\) and \(Y_{xx}(a)\neq 0\), then the vector on the right is
nonzero, so \(\mathbf\Pi\) is projectively immersive at \(a\), contradicting
accumulation of secant shadows there. Hence
\[
Y_{xx}(a)=0.
\]
On the \(v_5\)-patch,
\[
J_\lambda=\frac{M^3}{c^3}S_{xx},
\qquad
J_{u_5}=\frac{M^3}{c^3}Y_{xx},
\]
so \(K_v(a)=0\) implies \(J_\lambda(a)=0\), and the displayed vanishing of
\(Y_{xx}(a)\) gives \(J_{u_5}(a)=0\).
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Simple septic-zero fixed-shear branches off \(K_v=0\) transfer to nonmixed four-point geometry]
\label{cor:fixed-shear-simple-septic-zero-off-Kv-transfers-to-nonmixed-four-point}
Work on the overlap patch of
Proposition~\ref{prop:fixed-shear-overlap-branch-off-Kv-forces-fold-at-S-zero}.
Assume there is a close exact fixed-shear mixed \(2\)-point branch
\[
x_{1,n}\neq x_{2,n},
\qquad
x_{1,n},x_{2,n}\to a,
\qquad
\Phi(x_{1,n})=\Phi(x_{2,n}),
\]
and
\[
K_v(a)\neq 0.
\]
Then, after shrinking to a sufficiently small neighborhood of \(a\), this lane
produces a local interval-persistent nonmixed \(4\)-point family for the lifted
curve
\[
Q(x)=(x,Y(x),S(x)).
\]
Consequently it is absorbed by the existing nonmixed \(4\)-point theory;
in particular, it is not a surviving genuinely mixed \(2\)-point
derivative-geometric obstruction.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
By Proposition~\ref{prop:fixed-shear-overlap-branch-off-Kv-forces-fold-at-S-zero},
\[
S(a)=0,
\qquad
S_x(a)\neq 0,
\]
and the first coordinate of the fixed-shear projected germ is in fold normal
form. Thus, after analytic source reparametrization, there is a local parameter
\(t\) with
\[
\Phi(x(t))=(t^2,\mathcal V(t))
\]
and repeated nearby values force
\[
\mathcal V(t)=\mathcal V(-t)
\]
for all sufficiently small \(t\). Equivalently, in the actual local septic
coordinate \(s:=S\), there are even analytic germs \(E_x,E_Y\) such that
\[
\frac{x(s)-\xi_*s}{1-\eta_*s}=E_x(s),
\qquad
\frac{Y(s)-\gamma_*s}{1-\eta_*s}=E_Y(s),
\qquad
E_x(-s)=E_x(s),\quad E_Y(-s)=E_Y(s).
\]

Define
\[
Q(s):=(x(s),Y(s),s).
\]
If \(\eta_*\neq 0\), set
\[
P:=\left(\frac{\xi_*}{\eta_*},\frac{\gamma_*}{\eta_*},\frac1{\eta_*}\right).
\]
Then the parity formulas imply that \(Q(s),Q(-s),P\) are collinear for all
small \(s\). If \(\eta_*=0\), then
\[
Q(s)-Q(-s)=2s(\xi_*,\gamma_*,1),
\]
so all symmetric secants are parallel to one fixed direction, which is the same
projective statement with a point at infinity. Hence for every small
\(0<s_1<s_2\), the four points
\[
Q(-s_2),\ Q(-s_1),\ Q(s_1),\ Q(s_2)
\]
are coplanar.

Finally, by Proposition~\ref{prop:fixed-shear-overlap-branch-off-Kv-forces-fold-at-S-zero},
\[
x_s(a)=\frac{1}{S_x(a)}\neq 0,
\]
so \(x\) is monotone in \(s\) near \(a\). Thus the four coplanar points above
lie on one local \(x\)-arc in the nonmixed ordered pattern, yielding a local
interval-persistent nonmixed \(4\)-point family. The final claim follows from
Proposition~\ref{prop:interval-persistent-nonmixed-four-point-forces-affine-planarity}.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Status of the mixed \(\lambda\)-shear route]
\label{rem:wip-mixed-lambda-shear-route-status}

secant shadow
\[
\mathbf\Sigma(h_1,h_2)
=

\]
independently of any affine freezing of the branch-generated \(\lambda\)-shears.

There are now two useful sharpenings.

First,
Proposition~\ref{prop:off-septic-zero-Kv-accumulation-is-mixed-low-order}
shows that if a close mixed branch accumulates at a point with
\[
K_v=0,
\qquad
S\neq 0,
\]

\[

\[

\]
is not a surviving mixed \(2\)-point carrier lane: it transfers into a local
interval-persistent nonmixed \(4\)-point family and is therefore absorbed by
the existing nonmixed \(4\)-point theory.

Thus the derivative-geometric burden on the mixed two-point side is now sharply

\[

\]
itself. The remaining unresolved work is therefore:

derivative-geometric side, a proof that close mixed \(2\)-point accumulation on
\[
K_v=0
\]
is absorbed by the existing lifted \(3\)-point curvature/osculating machinery.
\end{remark}

\textbf{Two-point branch: three live conditional routes.}
The stronger finite-order route is still

data and satisfies swap symmetry, one-amplitude collapse, and diagonal merger
\[
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)=(a_1+a_2)F_h.
\]
The weaker exact route is
Proposition~\ref{prop:conditional-exact-two-point-exclusion-qabs}, which would
already remove exact close two-point bad cores on compact subsets of
\(\{c\neq 0\}\) from continuity and diagonal collapse of the actual corrected
two-atom quotient germ.

What is now ruled out is the naive source-summed corrected-block route: its
extracted one-atom finite-order coefficients are even in the source weight and
therefore cannot supply the required linear merger law. On the mixed side,
determinant-only and quotient-only arguments are likewise shear-blind. The
genuinely new derivative-geometric lane is the exact projective
\(\lambda\)-shear / secant-shadow route on a good overlap patch.

a close exact mixed two-point bad branch can accumulate only on
\[
\{S=0\}\cup\{K_v=0\},
\qquad

\]

\[
\{S=0\}\cap\{K_v\neq 0\}
\]
transfers into the established nonmixed \(4\)-point geometry.

quotient-diagonal continuity/diagonal collapse, or a proof that close mixed
two-point accumulation on
\[
K_v=0
\]
is absorbed by the existing lifted \(3\)-point curvature/osculating machinery.

1) Insert the missing proposition + corollary

Insert this block immediately after

\end{proof}

for

\begin{proposition}[Exact fixed-shear overlap branches off $K_v=0$ force a fold at $S=0$]
\label{prop:fixed-shear-overlap-branch-off-Kv-forces-fold-at-S-zero}

Use:

\begin{proposition}[Off-septic-zero $K_v$-accumulation is already mixed low-order]
\label{prop:off-septic-zero-Kv-accumulation-is-mixed-low-order}
Work on the overlap patch of
Proposition~\ref{prop:conditional-mixed-lambda-shear-projective-shadow-reduction}.
Assume there exists a close exact mixed two-point bad branch accumulating at a
point \(a\) such that
\[
K_v(a)=0,
\qquad
S(a)\neq 0.
\]
Then
\[
Y_{xx}(a)=0.
\]
Equivalently, on the \(v_5\)-patch one has
\[
J_\lambda(a)=0,
\qquad
J_{u_5}(a)=0.
\]
So any such accumulation already lies in the existing mixed low-order
obstruction regime.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By Proposition~\ref{prop:conditional-mixed-lambda-shear-projective-shadow-reduction},
any close exact mixed two-point bad branch determines the tangent shadow
\[
\mathbf\Pi(x)=[xS_x-S:\ YS_x-SY_x:\ S_x]
\]
with projective immersion defect
\[
\mathbf\Pi(x)\wedge \partial_x\mathbf\Pi(x)
=
S(x)\bigl(S_xY_{xx}-S_{xx}Y_x,\ S_{xx},\ -S_{xx}\bigr).
\]
At a point \(a\) with \(K_v(a)=0\), one has \(S_{xx}(a)=0\) on the \(v_5\)-patch,
so this simplifies to
\[
\mathbf\Pi(a)\wedge \partial_x\mathbf\Pi(a)
=
S(a)\,Y_{xx}(a)\,\bigl(S_x(a),\,0,\,S(a)-x(a)S_x(a)\bigr).
\]
If \(S(a)\neq 0\) and \(Y_{xx}(a)\neq 0\), then the vector on the right is
nonzero, so \(\mathbf\Pi\) is projectively immersive at \(a\), contradicting
accumulation of secant shadows there. Hence
\[
Y_{xx}(a)=0.
\]
On the \(v_5\)-patch,
\[
J_\lambda=\frac{M^3}{c^3}S_{xx},
\qquad
J_{u_5}=\frac{M^3}{c^3}Y_{xx},
\]
so \(K_v(a)=0\) implies \(J_\lambda(a)=0\), and the displayed vanishing of
\(Y_{xx}(a)\) gives \(J_{u_5}(a)=0\).
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Simple septic-zero fixed-shear branches off $K_v=0$ transfer to nonmixed four-point geometry]
\label{cor:fixed-shear-simple-septic-zero-off-Kv-transfers-to-nonmixed-four-point}
Work on the overlap patch of
Proposition~\ref{prop:fixed-shear-overlap-branch-off-Kv-forces-fold-at-S-zero}.
Assume there is a close exact fixed-shear mixed \(2\)-point branch
\[
x_{1,n}\neq x_{2,n},
\qquad
x_{1,n},x_{2,n}\to a,
\qquad
\Phi(x_{1,n})=\Phi(x_{2,n}),
\]
and
\[
K_v(a)\neq 0.
\]
Then, after shrinking to a sufficiently small neighborhood of \(a\), this lane
produces a local interval-persistent nonmixed \(4\)-point family for the lifted
curve
\[
Q(x)=(x,Y(x),S(x)).
\]
Consequently it is absorbed by the existing nonmixed \(4\)-point theory;
in particular, it is not a surviving genuinely mixed \(2\)-point
derivative-geometric obstruction.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
By Proposition~\ref{prop:fixed-shear-overlap-branch-off-Kv-forces-fold-at-S-zero},
\[
S(a)=0,
\qquad
S_x(a)\neq 0,
\]
and the first coordinate of the fixed-shear projected germ is in fold normal
form. Thus, after analytic source reparametrization, there is a local parameter
\(t\) with
\[
\Phi(x(t))=(t^2,\mathcal V(t))
\]
and repeated nearby values force
\[
\mathcal V(t)=\mathcal V(-t)
\]
for all sufficiently small \(t\). Equivalently, in the actual local septic
coordinate \(s:=S\), there are even analytic germs \(E_x,E_Y\) such that
\[
\frac{x(s)-\xi_*s}{1-\eta_*s}=E_x(s),
\qquad
\frac{Y(s)-\gamma_*s}{1-\eta_*s}=E_Y(s),
\qquad
E_x(-s)=E_x(s),\quad E_Y(-s)=E_Y(s).
\]

Define
\[
Q(s):=(x(s),Y(s),s).
\]
If \(\eta_*\neq 0\), set
\[
P:=\left(\frac{\xi_*}{\eta_*},\frac{\gamma_*}{\eta_*},\frac1{\eta_*}\right).
\]
Then the parity formulas imply that \(Q(s),Q(-s),P\) are collinear for all
small \(s\). If \(\eta_*=0\), then
\[
Q(s)-Q(-s)=2s(\xi_*,\gamma_*,1),
\]
so all symmetric secants are parallel to one fixed direction, which is the same
projective statement with a point at infinity. Hence for every small
\(0<s_1<s_2\), the four points
\[
Q(-s_2),\ Q(-s_1),\ Q(s_1),\ Q(s_2)
\]
are coplanar.

Finally, by Proposition~\ref{prop:fixed-shear-overlap-branch-off-Kv-forces-fold-at-S-zero},
\[
x_s(a)=\frac{1}{S_x(a)}\neq 0,
\]
so \(x\) is monotone in \(s\) near \(a\). Thus the four coplanar points above
lie on one local \(x\)-arc in the nonmixed ordered pattern, yielding a local
interval-persistent nonmixed \(4\)-point family. The final claim follows from
Proposition~\ref{prop:interval-persistent-nonmixed-four-point-forces-affine-planarity}.
\end{proof}

\end{proof}

for

\begin{proposition}[Exact fixed-shear overlap branches off $K_v=0$ force a fold at $S=0$]
\label{prop:fixed-shear-overlap-branch-off-Kv-forces-fold-at-S-zero}

Use:

\begin{proposition}[Off-septic-zero $K_v$-accumulation is already mixed low-order]
\label{prop:off-septic-zero-Kv-accumulation-is-mixed-low-order}
Work on the overlap patch of
Proposition~\ref{prop:conditional-mixed-lambda-shear-projective-shadow-reduction}.
Assume there exists a close exact mixed two-point bad branch accumulating at a
point \(a\) such that
\[
K_v(a)=0,
\qquad
S(a)\neq 0.
\]
Then
\[
Y_{xx}(a)=0.
\]
Equivalently, on the \(v_5\)-patch one has
\[
J_\lambda(a)=0,
\qquad
J_{u_5}(a)=0.
\]
So any such accumulation already lies in the existing mixed low-order
obstruction regime.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By Proposition~\ref{prop:conditional-mixed-lambda-shear-projective-shadow-reduction},
any close exact mixed two-point bad branch determines the tangent shadow
\[
\mathbf\Pi(x)=[xS_x-S:\ YS_x-SY_x:\ S_x]
\]
with projective immersion defect
\[
\mathbf\Pi(x)\wedge \partial_x\mathbfPi(x)
=
S(x)\bigl(S_xY_{xx}-S_{xx}Y_x,\ S_{xx},\ -S_{xx}\bigr).
\]
At a point \(a\) with \(K_v(a)=0\), one has \(S_{xx}(a)=0\) on the \(v_5\)-patch,
so this simplifies to
\[
\mathbf\Pi(a)\wedge \partial_x\mathbf\Pi(a)
=
S(a)\,Y_{xx}(a)\,\bigl(S_x(a),\,0,\,S(a)-x(a)S_x(a)\bigr).
\]
If \(S(a)\neq 0\) and \(Y_{xx}(a)\neq 0\), then the vector on the right is
nonzero, so \(\mathbf\Pi\) is projectively immersive at \(a\), contradicting
accumulation of secant shadows there. Hence
\[
Y_{xx}(a)=0.
\]
On the \(v_5\)-patch,
\[
J_\lambda=\frac{M^3}{c^3}S_{xx},
\qquad
J_{u_5}=\frac{M^3}{c^3}Y_{xx},
\]
so \(K_v(a)=0\) implies \(J_\lambda(a)=0\), and the displayed vanishing of
\(Y_{xx}(a)\) gives \(J_{u_5}(a)=0\).
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Simple septic-zero fixed-shear branches off $K_v=0$ transfer to nonmixed four-point geometry]
\label{cor:fixed-shear-simple-septic-zero-off-Kv-transfers-to-nonmixed-four-point}
Work on the overlap patch of
Proposition~\ref{prop:fixed-shear-overlap-branch-off-Kv-forces-fold-at-S-zero}.
Assume there is a close exact fixed-shear mixed \(2\)-point branch
\[
x_{1,n}\neq x_{2,n},
\qquad
x_{1,n},x_{2,n}\to a,
\qquad
\Phi(x_{1,n})=\Phi(x_{2,n}),
\]
and
\[
K_v(a)\neq 0.
\]
Then, after shrinking to a sufficiently small neighborhood of \(a\), this lane
produces a local interval-persistent nonmixed \(4\)-point family for the lifted
curve
\[
Q(x)=(x,Y(x),S(x)).
\]
Consequently it is absorbed by the existing nonmixed \(4\)-point theory;
in particular, it is not a surviving genuinely mixed \(2\)-point
derivative-geometric obstruction.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
By Proposition~\ref{prop:fixed-shear-overlap-branch-off-Kv-forces-fold-at-S-zero},
\[
S(a)=0,
\qquad
S_x(a)\neq 0,
\]
and the first coordinate of the fixed-shear projected germ is in fold normal
form. Thus, after analytic source reparametrization, there is a local parameter
\(t\) with
\[
\Phi(x(t))=(t^2,\mathcal V(t))
\]
and repeated nearby values force
\[
\mathcal V(t)=\mathcal V(-t)
\]
for all sufficiently small \(t\). Equivalently, in the actual local septic
coordinate \(s:=S\), there are even analytic germs \(E_x,E_Y\) such that
\[
\frac{x(s)-\xi_*s}{1-\eta_*s}=E_x(s),
\qquad
\frac{Y(s)-\gamma_*s}{1-\eta_*s}=E_Y(s),
\qquad
E_x(-s)=E_x(s),\quad E_Y(-s)=E_Y(s).
\]

Define
\[
Q(s):=(x(s),Y(s),s).
\]
If \(\eta_*\neq 0\), set
\[
P:=\left(\frac{\xi_*}{\eta_*},\frac{\gamma_*}{\eta_*},\frac1{\eta_*}\right).
\]
Then the parity formulas imply that \(Q(s),Q(-s),P\) are collinear for all
small \(s\). If \(\eta_*=0\), then
\[
Q(s)-Q(-s)=2s(\xi_*,\gamma_*,1),
\]
so all symmetric secants are parallel to one fixed direction, which is the same
projective statement with a point at infinity. Hence for every small
\(0<s_1<s_2\), the four points
\[
Q(-s_2),\ Q(-s_1),\ Q(s_1),\ Q(s_2)
\]
are coplanar.

Finally, by Proposition~\ref{prop:fixed-shear-overlap-branch-off-Kv-forces-fold-at-S-zero},
\[
x_s(a)=\frac{1}{S_x(a)}\neq 0,
\]
so \(x\) is monotone in \(s\) near \(a\). Thus the four coplanar points above
lie on one local \(x\)-arc in the nonmixed ordered pattern, yielding a local
interval-persistent nonmixed \(4\)-point family. The final claim follows from
Proposition~\ref{prop:interval-persistent-nonmixed-four-point-forces-affine-planarity}.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Exact shadow-adapted freezing on the simple septic-zero slice]
\label{rem:exact-shadow-adapted-freezing-simple-septic-zero}
Work on a good overlap patch and suppose
\[
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}
\]
is a local coordinate near a simple septic-zero point \(a\), so
\[
S(a)=0,
\qquad
S_x(a)\neq 0.
\]
Write \(s:=S\) and let
\[
C(s):=(x(s),Y(s)),
\qquad
x=\frac{v_5}{c},
\qquad
Y=\frac{u_5}{c}.
\]
For any distinct nearby secant pair \(s_1\neq s_2\), define
\[
\xi(s_1,s_2):=\frac{x(s_1)-x(s_2)}{s_1-s_2},
\qquad
\gamma(s_1,s_2):=\frac{Y(s_1)-Y(s_2)}{s_1-s_2}.
\]
Then one has the exact identities
\[
x(s_1)-\xi(s_1,s_2)\,s_1
=
x(s_2)-\xi(s_1,s_2)\,s_2,
\]
\[
Y(s_1)-\gamma(s_1,s_2)\,s_1
=
Y(s_2)-\gamma(s_1,s_2)\,s_2.
\]
Equivalently, on the simple septic-zero slice every exact secant-shadow pair
already carries an exact fixed-shear normalization with
\[
\eta=0,
\qquad
\xi=\xi(s_1,s_2),
\qquad
\gamma=\gamma(s_1,s_2).
\]

Thus the apparently projective, non-affinely-frozen septic-zero lane is not a
separate carrier mechanism on the simple \(S=0\) slice: in the shadow-adapted
chart it freezes exactly and therefore falls under the same exact fixed-shear
analysis used in
Corollary~\ref{cor:fixed-shear-simple-septic-zero-off-Kv-transfers-to-nonmixed-four-point}.
\end{remark}

4. Key Structural Findings and Goodies

This section reviews key results and structural findings from the work:

    Exact Projective Secant-Shadow Reduction: The projective secant-shadow is exact and independent of moving shears and őõőõ, forming the backbone of the entire attack. It is more powerful than the affine freeze, and it is essential to reducing the complexity of the mixed 22-point geometry.

    Secant-Shadow Normal Form: The normalized form of the secant-shadow map is:
    P~X(u,v)=X~0+B(ŌÉ)+ŌĄA(ŌÉ,ŌĄ),P~Z(u,v)=Z~0+ŌÉŌĄC(ŌÉ,ŌĄ),
    P
    X‚Äč(u,v)=X
    0‚Äč+B(ŌÉ)+ŌĄA(ŌÉ,ŌĄ),P
    Z‚Äč(u,v)=Z
    0‚Äč+ŌÉŌĄC(ŌÉ,ŌĄ),

    where B(ŌÉ)=brŌÉr+O(ŌÉr+1)B(ŌÉ)=br‚ÄčŌÉr+O(ŌÉr+1) and C(w)=c‚Ąďw‚Ąď+O(w‚Ąď+1)C(w)=c‚Ąď‚Äčw‚Ąď+O(w‚Ąď+1). This is the essential structure we work with for the residual Kv=0Kv‚Äč=0 lane.

    Tangent-Normalized Lane with Scalar Even Drift: The residual Kv=0Kv‚Äč=0 lane reduces to a single scalar even drift function BB. If B‚Č°Őł0BÓÄ†‚Č°0, then the secant-shadow map is locally injective for small ŌÉŌÉ and ŌĄŌĄ, as shown in the proposition.

    Critical Scaling: The only remaining unresolved regime for a surviving branch is when ŌĄ=őļŌÉr+o(ŌÉr)ŌĄ=őļŌÉr+o(ŌÉr), with őļőļ being a constant. Any value of őļőļ other than őļ=‚ąíbra0(‚Ąď+1)őļ=‚ąía0‚Äč(‚Ąď+1)br‚Äč‚Äč results in local injectivity of the map, which forces the branch to disappear.

    Exact Symmetric Shrinking Lifted 3-Point Circuits: If B‚Č°0B‚Č°0, the branch transfers to exact symmetric shrinking lifted 3-point circuits, completing the transfer to the nonmixed 3-point geometry.

5. Known Limitations and Key Negative Findings
